It is hard to even find a 100% badger brush for the price of this kit.  A number of them start at double what this kit costs.  So you can almost think of it as just getting the cup, soap, and stand for free!     <li> Pluses:  -The brush stand holds a razor as well  -The soap is surprisingly nice. Very mild and very easy to lather.  -The bowl is easy to use with any type of soap and is a nice, heavy, ceramic bowl  -Badger brush feels great and lathers well with any type of soap  Minuses:  -The badger brush lost a bit of hair in the beginning, but I think this is pretty normal. Since the first use, I have noticed significant hair loss from the brush, just the occasional bristle here and there.  Lather:  The lather was very easy to work up. By adding water incrementally to the bowl with the brush, and working the brush in a circular motion in the bowl, I was able to build up a nice lather on the brush. The brush then washes really easily--it really is more like hair than I thought it would be. The soap that comes in the set doesn&#x27;t have much (if any) fragrance, and is super mild.  Brush:  The brush is great. Before the first time I used it, I shampooed it as I had read about somewhere with the shampoo I regularly use. Don&#x27;t know if this made any difference but it was easy to do. I tend to rinse the brush thoroughly in warm water before I use it, and flick any excess water out. If I need additional water to get a good lather, I just put water in the soap bowl or rinse the brush a bit more. I hesitate from using super hot water because I&#x27;m not sure what it would do to the bristles.  Shave prep:  I just take a hot shower and use a mild face cleanser. I don&#x27;t use any pre-shave oil, and I use a plain moisturizer instead of an aftershave.</li>

I look forward to trying a different soap when the included one is used up and perhaps upgrading the stand, too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;***Brush rinsing tip***&lt;br /&gt;So, you&#x27;re supposed to rinse out all the soap and dry the brush as best as you can when you&#x27;re done, so here&#x27;s what I found to be the most efficient way:&lt;br /&gt;-Start by gently shaking and rotating the brush under fairly high faucet pressure.&lt;br /&gt;-Splay out the brush against the palm of your hand to increase the amount of bristles exposed to the water.  Don&#x27;t spread them by pulling the bristles apart with your fingers.&lt;br /&gt;-The brush should be thoroughly soaked at this point.  Immediately hold the brush upright(bristles on top) to prevent the water from dripping on your floor and go to your shower and vigorously shake the water out. Should only take a few shakes till the bristles look fairly dry and you don&#x27;t see any soap gathered at the tip.  Doing this in the shower will save you from the splatter mess that would otherwise occur on your bathroom counter and mirror (as I found out the first time).</li>

Most DE handles are 75mm (short) to 100mm (XL) long. Traditional is about 80-85mm.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would buy this set for a family member or friend looking into trying traditional DE shaving without hesitation, knowing they will likely move on in a few months.     <li> Recently I decided to go old-school with my shaving habits.     <li> I was introduced to wet shaving only months ago when, for Father&#x27;s Day, my son surprised me with the Van Der Hagen Men&#x27;s Luxury Shave Kit, an [[ASIN:B003LW4LJK Edwin Jagger De86bl Faux Ebony Double Edge Safety Razor, Black]] and some [[ASIN:B001OXTHJC Astra Superior Platinum Double Edge Razor Blades - 30 Ct]] blades.     <li> This is a great kit for beginners who want to dip their feet into wet shaving, but aren&#x27;t prepared to spend a lot of money.  Unfortunately in this case, you get what you pay for. On top of this, I do not believe this brush is 100% badger as described.  While this brush is reasonably soft, it is nowhere near as soft as many badger brushes I&#x27;ve felt since this purchase.  The brush is well constructed and feels good in your hand, but it is not a joy to actually use.  The hairs are a bit coarse and tend to poke at the skin.  I&#x27;ve since dropped $30 on a true badger brush.    The soap smells great, but is a trick to lather.  A tiny amount of water on the brush will result in a thin, bubbly foam that doesn&#x27;t coat the skin well.  But no water on the brush, and the soap won&#x27;t lather at all.  After two months of practice I still haven&#x27;t gotten the hang of it.  Maybe it&#x27;s just me, but I&#x27;ve ordered a different brand of soap to try.     <li> good smells creamy smooth</li>
    <li> This is a great set for the price.  A couple of notes though:  First, this set includes a \\&quot;pure badger\\&quot; brush.  This is the lowest grade of badger hair (higher grades, in ascending order are \\&quot;fine badger\\&quot; and \\&quot;silvertip badger\\&quot;) and often has the tips cut off in order to form the brush shape.  If the tips are cut the brush won&#x27;t wear in as well, so I was hoping this wasn&#x27;t the case but it is.  Given this, the brush is a little scratchy and will stay that way.  The upside is that it works up a very good lather, but I wouldn&#x27;t recommend this for anyone with sensitive skin.  Second, the apothecary mug is meant to have the soap left in the bottom.  The soap that&#x27;s included has a pleasant mild scent, lathers up well, and fits nicely into the mug, so that&#x27;s nice.  However, you might have difficulty using other soaps with it and the remaining space is difficult to work up enough lather in.  It would be nice if it were a little taller and tapered out further with a milder slant.  For the price and what&#x27;s included, it&#x27;s still a great set.     <li> UPDATE 12/4/2013: The brush with this starter set fell apart the other day, so I&#x27;m adding this comment to report what happened.  Be aware that the brush is actually constructed using a wax-like glue to hold the bristles together at its base.  The brush has a metal ring around its base, and this is inserted into the handle.  Glue is applied around the bottom of the bristles to hold it in the handle.  This quality of construction is poor.  Most people soak their brush in hot water before shaving.  With this type of brush construction, soaking the brush in hot water loosens the glue, making it prone to failure.  For this reason, I&#x27;m downgrading my rating for this item from four stars to three stars.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you purchase this set, do not use your hand to squeeze excess water out of the brush.  Doing so can pull the bristles and wax out of the handle.  Rather, shake the brush to remove extra water.  Treat the brush gently to ensure the assembly remains intact.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A quality brush uses knots, not wax, to hold the bristles together.  With this brush, you&#x27;ll notice some badger hairs will fall out, over time.  Given the low price of this set, I still see it as a nice starter for those new to wet shaving.  Just be aware that you&#x27;ll probably want or need to replace the brush eventually.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The following is my original review.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;------------------------------------&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Getting started with a safety razor can be an expensive proposition. You have the razor, which can set you back anywhere between $35 for a cheapy to $300 or more for a high-quality shaver. You have the cup, the soap, the brush, the shaver and brush holder, the balms, salves, creams, lotions. OMG! If you&#x27;re like me, you want to save money and not have to spend a fortune on replacement razors for your store-bought shaver. The good news is that all these things are a one-time expense. Once you&#x27;re up and running, the price of quality blades is where you&#x27;ll save your money to pay for all these other items, over time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Van Der Hagen shave set gives you everything you need to get started, sans shaver, at a very reasonable price. It&#x27;s a starter set for those new to this form of shaving, and it can be used by those experienced also.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The set comes with a ceramic cup that nicely houses the supplied soap cake. The cup size supports many other manufactured soap cakes also. The cup handle is a little small for those of us with large hands, so if you have large hands, you may want to wrap your digits securely around the entire cup, lest the little handle slips out from between your soapy fingers. A badger brush is provided that is of acceptable quality, although if you take to this form of shaving, you&#x27;ll probably want to upgrade the brush, in time. A stylish, thick, transparent plastic holder has cutouts to hold the brush and your razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve been using this set for a few weeks now and like it. It does what it&#x27;s intended to do and doesn&#x27;t break the bank. The quality of the soap is adequate, although it lacks the slickness I can get from other brands of soap, but it&#x27;s perfectly acceptable. It&#x27;s easy on my skin and leaves a mild, clean scent that isn&#x27;t overpowering.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you&#x27;re looking for a starter set and are beginning your ventures into the relaxing world of wet shaving, I&#x27;d definitely recommend the Van Der Hagen shave set. In time, I plan to upgrade the brush, but for now, this is fine. I&#x27;m definitely going to change the soap cake to something with more slickness. What&#x27;s nice about this set is that it&#x27;s a one-stop purchase for those who want to get started with the basic essentials at a reasonable price.or all these other items, over time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Van Der Hagen shave set gives you everything you need to get started, sans shaver, at a very reasonable price. It&#x27;s a starter set for those new to this form of shaving, and it can be used by those experienced also.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The set comes with a ceramic cup that nicely houses the supplied soap cake.     <li> So i received this kit on Apr 2, 2013, and i like it.&lt;br /&gt;When I first opened the box, the stand came out broken at the top (although there was no visible damage to the exterior of the box), but a little superglue at the joint took care of it pretty well, and is still holding strong today (4 months later).&lt;br /&gt;The apothecary mug is great; it looks fantastic as part of the decor, and the finish holds up really well and cleans easily.&lt;br /&gt;The soap it came with smells pretty good, although i may go with a different brand, just to get a sense of different lathers and textures and smells.     <li> I&#x27;m new to DE shaving, and when making the initial investment, buying a starter-kit seemed to make a lot of financial sense.  Every site that I referenced during my research said that you should invest in a badger hair brush.  This kit has one, and the price certainly is very reasonable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;**The Brush**&lt;br /&gt;This brush is 100% pure badger hair.  It&#x27;s soft to the touch, and does a good job with lathering/applying the shave soap.  Some other reviewers had some complaints about loose hairs and an odor.  Well, a bit of quick research will tell you that you should expect to find a few hairs in the lather (in the bowl, or on your face) during the first several shaves, as you need to break in the brush.  These hairs were probably relatively  loose to begin with, but the manufacturer wasn&#x27;t able to remove them before shipping.  I also read that you can expect a few hairs to come out during the life of the brush - especially during the first few months after it breaks in.  If you have clumps falling out, then the product is defective.  In short, don&#x27;t worry if you see a few hairs here and there!  As far as the smell, well...  it&#x27;s made of animal hair, and it smells very faintly like wet animal after you wet it.  It&#x27;s not oppressive, and the soap that comes with this seems to cover it up.  Don&#x27;t worry...  if the faint odor is even remotely offensive, it&#x27;ll go away in a short while.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;**The Soap**&lt;br /&gt;The Van Der Hagen soap that comes in this kit if perfectly serviceable.     <li> Review:&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve used this for approximately one year now.  Yes I&#x27;ve been using the stand, brush and bowl for a year.  The soap it comes with is very mediocre, I found that out after mine had run out after a few months (wish my cans of shaving gel lasted that long!).  I&#x27;ve had fun since looking around Amazon for different soaps/creams and finding something I will most likely stick with for the rest of my shaving career.  The brush is a very nice one, I have a boars brush (boars brushes aren&#x27;t going to rip your face off) and another badger, apart from STILL shedding this one is my favorite.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I decided to ding it because of the soap and the still shedding brush, but I stand by my statement that this is the best box set to buy for when you are getting in to traditional, double-edge blade shaving.  Nothing beats having a ceramic bowl, brush and stand for this price.  Only way to make this better is by adding a Styptic Pencil.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Traditional Shaving:&lt;br /&gt;I have been upset with buying cartridge based shavers for years now:&lt;br /&gt;-  I&#x27;m required to shave daily for work, if I shave on Monday and its irritated that usually means by Friday my face is trying to run away from me.&lt;br /&gt;-  $50 for a set of 10 cartridges that will last me maybe 2 months, the base was $25 alone.  Since my purchase I realize the bases are now practically free.&lt;br /&gt;-  Cans of cream/gel/foam are messy and don&#x27;t last long.&lt;br /&gt;-  Shaving took me a long time due to the level of scruff I have under my jaw line.  Constantly clogging the cartridge and taking longer then expected to clean out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So I set out to find alternatives to this harsh reality us men have to go through!  I came across traditional DE shavers and thought man ... these are still a real thing? AWESOME!  I&#x27;ve learned quite a bit on my own in how to shave and that&#x27;s how I truly believe it should be with everyone.  Seeing as everyone has different skin, different hair, different growth they should figure out what works with them and their skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My recommendation is when you are first taking your baby steps into the magical land of Double Edge Safety Razor shaving, go slow, very slow.  Take that razor by the hilt, let it touch your skin without putting pressure on your razor and let it glide slowly down in one small motion and don&#x27;t go over the area again immediately.  Eventually you will figure out how fast you can go, angles to take, pressure applied (I don&#x27;t apply any!) and if you should go against the grain.  Also I find it helpful to change the blade immediately when I feel tugging.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Brushes and Lather:&lt;br /&gt;Soaps and Creams aren&#x27;t very different.  Creams take less time to make &#x27;thick&#x27; lather and often have very strong smells to them.  Soaps are tough bars that are usually placed in the bowl with hot water or rubbed in a face cloth to develop lather.  Pick your poison, I have both and chose the soap because its A) More fun and B) Doesn&#x27;t smell like Sex Panther.  To develop lather its comically easy; wet brush, stir brush in bowl that has soap in it  and apply suds.  Personal Preference: As I&#x27;m applying lather I would much rather have a &#x27;close&#x27; to solid white of foundation versus having the super thick foundation where I won&#x27;t see my skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for the brush, buy a few.  If this one isn&#x27;t cutting it for you there are tons of cheap ones available.  I really only bought the other 2 to see what other brushes were like.  Found out they are all very similar and why wouldn&#x27;t they be? I&#x27;m not buying a diamond studded brush for $200, all of mine are sub $10 and they did their job without removing my face from my body.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Opinion: All the bases are essentially the same.  I have a Merkur that transforms into a butterfly so you can let the blade go.  I also have a Parker that does the same thing, I find that all I wanted was the easily accessible razor blade.  Oh and razor blades, I dislike Merkur Razors.  Currently I&#x27;m going through a 100 pack of Astra and after that I&#x27;m going to try Feather.  Right now the Astra&#x27;s blow away the Merkur&#x27;s.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m really happy I have made the move, saved some money, learned something new, got a better shave and I&#x27;m having fun shaving now.  Its no longer a chore, I like building up my lather, I like that I have to think about shaving my face and plus its great when others find out you don&#x27;t use a Mach 5 to shave as if you were nuts or grew up in the gritty west!  I kept my Mach 3 set, its my backup and travel companion, since I heard they don&#x27;t like these razors going on planes.</li>

    <li> The brush fell apart within a few months. The bristle component dislodged from the handle and separated in two while I was shaking it to dry the bristles after a shave.     <li> I ordered this set, excited to get both a new soap and a decent badger brush.  I was very disappointed when I first opened the package and the cloying, synthetic-smelling flowery fragrance made me sneeze.  The badger brush is just a &amp;#34;best&amp;#34; and not a silver tip bristle knot, but it looked thick and good for whipping up lather.  The mug is heavy and has a little knob for your hand to hold it.  The stand is clear acrylic and very sturdy. This set LOOKS great, but the performance leaves much to be desired.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ALL badger brushes come from animals that are basically hunted wild in China (with licenses and a only a certain number each year taken in each season) so I expect the hair on the brush to have variation and also a little smell to it.  It&#x27;s usually advised to wash the brush in shaving soap for a bit, then rinse gently and dry it out.  But this brush had a horrible animal odor to it that was mixed with a formaldehyde or solvent smell that several washes couldn&#x27;t get rid of!  It was detectable over the scent of the soap (more on that horror in a bit) and lingered in my nostrils after shaving with my favorite soap.  Additionally, the brush lost a LOT of hairs (10 to 20) every time I tried to lather with it, rinse it or manipulate it in any way.  The knot is not secure enough in the handle and it shows.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The soap is another sad story.  It&#x27;s supposedly full of glycerin and oils, but the smell is so overpowering to me that my allergies flared up as soon as I lathered my face.  After my shave, I broke out in a rash over the places where the soap was.  I respond like that to some synthetic fragrances so I was very disappointed in the soap.  It seemed to need a LOT of work to make a good lather, too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This set is a good start but is NOT worth the money.  You are better off getting a NICE brush (I have several Edwin Jagger brushes, and they also make Crabtree&amp;Evelyn brushes!) and a GREAT soap like the New Proraso or even a really expensiveshea butter soap bar.  Woolfat soaps are also excellent. Here&#x27;s my rating in order of precedence.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;o The SOAP gets 5 stars --  The soap has a very pleasant scent, and even though it has cocoa butter in it, I can&#x27;t smell it (which is a plus for me).  The soap lathers really well, is very slick, and I actually got no nicks on my first shave.  It rinses very clean, and left me with a feeling on my skin that I usually get after using a toner.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;o  The BRUSH gets 4 stars -- The Brush did shed a little bit, which may be normal, but it did bother me a little bit.  Also, the bristles are very soft, which make it difficult to work an extremely thick lather.  However, it did allow me to work a lather that was very slick and protected my face; I just usually prefer heavier.  The scent of the badger brush isn&#x27;t overly powerful, and I&#x27;m sure it will wash out in a couple weeks (I shave daily).  Does the job, and is an attractive handle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;o  The STAND gets 4 Stars -- There&#x27;s no channeling on the stand for water runoff, which is the main reason (NOT A DEAL BREAKER).  Standing water breeds bacteria, so I didn&#x27;t like that.  It cleans very easily though, and holds my triple blade razor just fine.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;o The BOWL gets 5 Stars -- This bowl is large enough to accommodate other soaps, and not run over with lather.  The handle isn&#x27;t entirely ergonomic, but that&#x27;s not a big deal.  The porcelain finish is very smooth, and it looks great.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;o Not that you need to make a fashionstatement while shaving, but this kit looks great, and is just as functional.  I haven&#x27;t had it long, but I&#x27;m very impressed.  I&#x27;ve been using this with a 4 bladed razor, and it&#x27;s great.  I plan on purchasing a safety razor once I&#x27;m out of cartridges, so I&#x27;ll update my review then.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Thanks for reading, I hope this was helpful</li>

Considering that all of these items separately would add up to quite a bit more than what you&#x27;re paying for this seems like a smart choice for someone who is starting with nothing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I imagine that I&#x27;ll keep using the brush and holder for a few years. The soap I will replace when it runs out, probably with a different brand (only because I like to try new things).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am satisfied that my money was well spent and I would recommend this set to anyone who may be wondering where to start.</li>
    <li> So I&#x27;ve had this set for quite a while now and have decided to leave my review.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-- The Good&lt;br /&gt;  The Brush knot is nice and full, if a little too floppy.&lt;br /&gt;  The Soap smells nice and it&#x27;s fit is perfect for the mug.&lt;br /&gt;  The Mug is probably the best part of the set with the windmill printed on both sides.&lt;br /&gt;  The Stand works as it should and is a step-up from my home made wire-hanger brush stand.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-- The Bad&lt;br /&gt;  The brush is quite floppy and loses hair like mad. Just today over 40 hairs came out (worse than the Van Der Hagen boar brush and that&#x27;s saying something!)&lt;br /&gt;  The soap, while smelling wonderful, barely foams and goes on as thin as hand soap.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I really wanted to like this set as my favorite cheap brush is the Van Der Hagen boar brush (once it stops losing hair every shave and you soften it up, it works wonders for a boar brush.), but to say that this brush is low quality is insulting to low quality brushes, my $10 tweezerman badger brush works better, is less floppy, and hasn&#x27;t lost more than 15 hairs in its life time! This brush on the other hand, loses at least five hairs every shave. So today i decided to work out all the bad hairs I could from the knot, i got over 40 hairs to come out with little effort. Repeating the same process on my tweezerman yielded less than 4 hairs. For how long i&#x27;ve been using the brush it should have ceased to losing hairs at this point, and yet it still does. The soap smells decent, but when attempting to lather all I ever get is foam! Granted, I have hard water, but i&#x27;ve so many different soaps and creams to compare from and this is by far the thinnest, least lubricating shaving soap I own, this even includes the lowest end Van Der Hagen soaps! The only good thing to come from this whole set is the mug.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All-in-all I&#x27;m very, very disappointed with this purchase. If you need a brush for cheap either go with the tweezerman badger hair or if you want a boar, and can deal with tons of hairs falling out of the knot, get the Van Der Hagen boar brush. What ever you do, do not waste your money on anything in this set except, maybe, the mug.</li>
    <li> For a beginner this is a great deal. For experienced shavers this is still a really good deal. The mug is heavy, feels sturdy and overall gives a nice in hand feel. The brush is good quality, but will lose a few hairs to start with, but I&#x27;m hard pressed to find brushes that don&#x27;t. Keep in mind it comes witha a Soap and not a Cream. A soap will lather marginally less but glide better, so keep that in mind. I am not the biggest fan of the plastic holder, but that&#x27;s because my razor is chrome and it doesn&#x27;t fit well with the look. Great kit otherwise.</li>

If you want a cheap brush, I recommend you replace the brush with something else like:  Omega Shaving Brush #10048 (chrome) or #10049 (black)  Very large boar brush with a huge knot, 28mm knot. Unclipped and will get softer with time.    Omega Shaving Brush #20102  Large boar brush with a 27mm knot. Unclipped and will get softer with time. Very comfortable handle.    Omega Shaving Brush #10065 (many colors to choose from) or #10066 (faux ivory)  Medium size boar brush, 24mm knot. Unclipped hairs that get softer with time.    Omega S-Brush #S10065 (many colors to choose from) or #S10019 (black and clear)  Medium size synthetic brush, 24mm knot. Not made from animal hair and thus very low maintenance. No break in required. Good firm feel but still very soft tips.    Vie-Long #12705  Medium size horse hair brush, 23mm knot. Horse hair is fairly soft. No break in required.    Semogue #1470 (wood handle) or #1460 (painted wood handle)  Small size boar brush, 21mm knot. Nice feel of the wood handle. The hairs are also unclipped and will get softer with time.    Notice I didn&#x27;t recommend any badger brushes? This is because there are virtually no good badger brushes in the $10-$20 price range. Good badger brushes start at around $30. Most good cheap brushes will be bore hair, horse hair, or synthetic.</li>
